           </i>
           =
           <a href="/wiki/Floor_and_ceiling_functions" title="Floor and ceiling functions">
            ⌊
           </a>
           <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">
             <i>
              year
             </i>
            </span>
            <span class="visualhide">
             /
            </span>
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">
             100
            </span>
           </span>
           ⌋
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = 17
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            p
           </i>
           = ⌊
           <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">
             13 + 8
             <i>
              k
             </i>
            </span>
            <span class="visualhide">
             /
            </span>
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">
             25
            </span>
           </span>
           ⌋
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            p
           </i>
           = 5
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            q
           </i>
           = ⌊
           <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">
             <i>
              k
             </i>
            </span>
            <span class="visualhide">
             /
            </span>
            <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">
             4
            </span>
           </span>
           ⌋
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            q
           </i>
           = 4
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = (15 −
           <i>
            p
           </i>
           +
           <i>

           </i>
           −
           <i>
            q
           </i>
           ) mod 30
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = 23
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = (4 +
           <i>
            k
           </i>
           −
           <i>

           </i>
           ) mod 7
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = 3
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>

           </i>
           = (19
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           +
           <i>
            M
           </i>
           ) mod 30
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 3
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           = (2
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           + 4
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           + 6
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           +
           <i>
            N
           </i>
           ) mod 7
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           = 5
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           Gregorian Easter is 22 +
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           +
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           March or
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           +
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           − 9 April
          </td>
          <td>
           30 March
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2">
           if
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 29 and
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           = 6, replace 26 April with 19 April
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2">
           if
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 28,
           <i>
            e
           </i>
           = 6, and (11
           <i>
            M
           </i>
           + 11) mod 30 &lt; 19, replace 25 April with 18 April
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2">
           For the Julian Easter in the Julian calendar
           <i>
            M
           </i>
           = 15 and
           <i>
            N
           </i>
           = 6 (
           <i>
            k
           </i>
           ,
           <i>
            p
           </i>
           , and
           <i>
            q
           </i>
           are unnecessary)
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       An analysis of the Gauss Easter Sunday algorithm is divided into two parts. The first part is the approximate tracking of the lunar orbiting and the second one is the exact, deterministic offsetting to obtain a Sunday following the full moon.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first part consists of determining the variable
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       , the number of days (counting from March 22) for the closest following full moon to occur. The formula for
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       contains the terms 19
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       and the constant M.
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       is the year's position in the 19-year lunar phase cycle, in which by assumption the moon's movement relative to earth repeats every 19 calendar years. In older times, 19 calendar years were equated to 235 lunar months (the Metonic cycle), which is remarkably close since 235 lunar months are approximately 6939.6813 days and 19 years are on average 6939.6075 days. The expression (19
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       + M) mod 30 repeats every 19 years within each century as M is determined per century. The 19-year cycle has nothing to do with the '19' in 19
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       , it is just a coincidence that another '19' appears. The '19' in 19
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       comes from correcting the mismatch between a calendar year and an integer number of lunar months. A calendar year (non-leap year) has 365 days and the closest you can come with an integer number of lunar months is
       <span class="nowrap">
        12 × 29.5 = 354
       </span>
       days. The difference is 11 days, which must be corrected for by moving the following year's occurrence of a full moon 11 days back. But in modulo 30 arithmetic, subtracting 11 is the same as adding 19, hence the addition of 19 for each year added, i.e. 19
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The M in
       <span class="nowrap">
        19
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        + M
       </span>
       serves to have a correct starting point at the start of each century. It is determined by a calculation taking the number of leap years up until that century where
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       inhibits a leap day every 100 years and
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       reinstalls it every 400 years, yielding
       <span class="nowrap">
        (
        <i>
         k
        </i>
        −
        <i>
         q
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       as the total number of inhibitions to the pattern of a leap day every four years. Thus we add
       <span class="nowrap">
        (
        <i>
         k
        </i>
        −
        <i>
         q
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       to correct for leap days that never occurred.
       <i>
        p
       </i>
       corrects for the lunar orbit not being fully describable in integer terms.
      </p>
      <p>
       The range of days considered for the full moon to determine Easter are 22 March to 20 April—a 30-day range mirrored in the mod 30 arithmetic of variable
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       and constant
       <i>
        M
       </i>
       , both of which can have integer values in the range 0 to 29. Once
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       is determined, this is the number of days to add to 22 March (the earliest full moon allowed by the date range) to obtain the day of the full moon.
      </p>
      <p>
       The second part is finding
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       , the additional offset days that must be added to the date offset
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       to make it arrive at a Sunday. Since the week has 7 days, the offset must be in the range 0 to 6 and determined by modulo 7 arithmetic.
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       is determined by calculating
       <span class="nowrap">
        2
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        + 4
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        + 6
        <i>
         d
        </i>
        +
        <i>
         N
        </i>
        mod 7
       </span>
       . These constants may seem strange at first, but are quite easily explainable if we remember that we operate under mod 7 arithmetic. To begin with,
       <span class="nowrap">
        2
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        + 4
        <i>
         c
        </i>
       </span>
       ensures that we take care of the fact that weekdays slide for each year. A normal year has 365 days, but
       <span class="nowrap">
        52 × 7 = 364
       </span>
       , so 52 full weeks make up one day too little. Hence, each consecutive year, the weekday "slides one day forward", meaning if May 6 was a Wednesday one year, it is a Thursday the following year (disregarding leap years). Both
       <i>
        b
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        c
       </i>
       increases by one for an advancement of one year (disregarding modulo effects). The expression
       <span class="nowrap">
        2
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        + 4
        <i>
         c
        </i>
       </span>
       thus increases by 6—but remember that this is the same as subtracting 1 mod 7. And to subtract by 1 is exactly what is required for a normal year – since the weekday slips one day forward we should compensate one day less to arrive at the correct weekday (i.e. Sunday). For a leap year,
       <i>
        b
       </i>
       becomes 0 and 2
       <i>
        b
       </i>
       thus is 0 instead of 8—which under mod 7, is another subtraction by 1—i.e., a total subtraction by 2, as the weekdays after the leap day that year slides forward by two days.
      </p>
      <p>
       The expression 6
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       works the same way. Increasing
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       by some number
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       indicates that the full moon occurs y days later this year, and hence we should compensate y days less. Adding 6
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       is mod 7 the same as subtracting
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       , which is the desired operation. Thus, again, we do subtraction by adding under modulo arithmetic. In total, the variable
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       contains the step from the day of the full moon to the nearest following Sunday, between 0 and 6 days ahead. The constant
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       provides the starting point for the calculations for each century and depends on where Jan 1, year 1 was implicitly located when the Gregorian calendar was constructed.
      </p>
      <p>
       The expression
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         d
        </i>
        +
        <i>
         e
        </i>
       </span>
       can yield offsets in the range 0 to 35 pointing to possible Easter Sundays on March 22 to April 26. For reasons of historical compatibility, all offsets of 35 and some of 34 are subtracted by 7, jumping one Sunday back to the day before the full moon (in effect using a negative
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       of −1). This means that 26 April is never Easter Sunday and that 19 April is overrepresented. These latter corrections are for historical reasons only and has nothing to do with the mathematical algorithm.
      </p>
      <p>
       Using the Gauss algorithm for years prior to 1583 is historically pointless since the Gregorian calendar was not utilised for determining Easter before that year. Using the algorithm far into the future is questionable, since we know nothing about how different churches will define Easter that far ahead. Easter calculations are based on agreements and conventions, not on the actual celestial movements nor on indisputable facts of history.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Anonymous_Gregorian_algorithm">
        Anonymous Gregorian algorithm
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Computus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Anonymous Gregorian algorithm">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       "A New York correspondent" submitted this algorithm for determining the Gregorian Easter to the journal
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">
         Nature
        </a>
       </i>
       in 1876.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bien_49-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bien-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has been reprinted many times, e.g., in 1877 by Samuel Butcher in
       <i>
        The Ecclesiastical Calendar
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butcher_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Butcher-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         225
        </span>
       </sup>
       in 1916 by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A._M._W._Downing" title="A. M. W. Downing">
        Arthur Downing
       </a>
       in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Observatory_(journal)" title="The Observatory (journal)">
         The Observatory
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1922 by
       <a href="/wiki/Harold_Spencer_Jones" title="Harold Spencer Jones">
        H. Spencer Jones
       </a>
       in
       <i>
        General Astronomy
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1977 by the
       <i>
        Journal of the British Astronomical Association
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1977 by
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Farmer%27s_Almanac" title="Old Farmer's Almanac">
        <i>
         The Old Farmer's Almanac
        </i>
       </a>
       , in 1988 by Peter Duffett-Smith in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Practical_Astronomy_with_your_Calculator" title="Practical Astronomy with your Calculator">
         Practical Astronomy with your Calculator
        </a>
       </i>
       , and in 1991 by
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Meeus" title="Jean Meeus">
        Jean Meeus
       </a>
       in
       <i>
        Astronomical Algorithms
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of the Meeus’ book citation, that is also called "Meeus/Jones/Butcher" algorithm:
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span id="Meeus.27_Julian_algorithm">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Meeus'_Julian_algorithm">
        Meeus' Julian algorithm
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Computus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Meeus' Julian algorithm">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Jean Meeus, in his book
       <i>
        Astronomical Algorithms
       </i>
       (1991, p. 69), presents the following algorithm for calculating the Julian Easter on the Julian Calendar, which is not the Gregorian Calendar used throughout the contemporary world; to obtain the date of Eastern Orthodox Easter on the latter calendar, 13 days (as of 1900 through 2099) must be added to the Julian dates, producing the dates below, in the last row.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <table class="wikitable">
         <tr>
          <th>
           Expression

          </th>

           <i>

           = 2016
          </th>
         </tr>

      <h4>
       <span id="Adaptation_for_Western_Easter_of_Meeus.27_Julian_algorithm">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Adaptation_for_Western_Easter_of_Meeus'_Julian_algorithm">
        Adaptation for Western Easter of Meeus' Julian algorithm
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Computus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Adaptation for Western Easter of Meeus' Julian algorithm">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Following is a method devised by Professor R. Sivaraman from Chennai, India a Mathematics Professor and Founder of Pie Mathematics Association, for finding Gregorian Western Easter date, which is now used by the majority of Christians, from 1900 to 2199.
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Let
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        be the remainder when the given year
        <i>
         Y
        </i>
        is divided by 19.
       </li>
       <li>
        Let
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        be the remainder when
        <span class="nowrap">
         11
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         + 5
        </span>
        is divided by 30.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="nowrap">
         <i>
          c
         </i>
         =
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         + 1
        </span>
        if either
        <span class="nowrap">
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         = 0
        </span>
        , or both
        <span class="nowrap">
         <i>
          b
         </i>
         = 1
        </span>
        and
        <span class="nowrap">
         <i>
          a
         </i>
         &gt; 10
        </span>
        ; otherwise
        <span class="nowrap">
         <i>
          c
         </i>
         =
         <i>
          b
         </i>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        If
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        is any value from 1 to 19, then the Easter Month is April and if it takes values from 20 to 29 then the Easter Month is March.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         d
        </i>
        is the remainder when
        <span class="nowrap">
         50 −
         <i>
          c
         </i>
        </span>
        is divided by 31.
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The date of Easter falls on the Sunday following the date
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       given by steps 4 and 5.
      </p>
      <p>
       As an illustration, let us consider the case for the year 2016. It is easy to check that
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        = 2
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         b
        </i>
        = 27
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        = 27
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         d
        </i>
        = 23
       </span>
       . Since
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         c
        </i>
        = 27
       </span>
       , by step 4, the Easter month was March and so the Easter date fell on Sunday following 23 March, which was 27 March. This is indeed correct, as the Gregorian Western Easter date fell on 27 March for the year 2016.
      </p>
      <p>
       We can find the Easter date for any given year from 2200 to 2299 by using the aforementioned formula by making the only little change in step 2. In this case,
       <i>
        b
       </i>
       is the remainder when
       <span class="nowrap">
        11
        <i>
         a
        </i>
        + 4
       </span>
       is divided by 30. Other details remain same as above.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <table class="wikitable">
         <tr>
          <th>
           Expression
          </th>
          <th style="text-align: left;">
           Y = 1913 - 1900
          </th>
          <th style="text-align: left;">
           Y = 2038 - 2000
          </th>
          <th style="text-align: left;">
           Y = 2106 - 2100
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           = (Y + M) mod 19
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           = 13 (M = 0)
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           = 5 (M = 5)
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           = 16 (M = 10)
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           = (11
           <i>
            a
           </i>
           + 5) mod 30
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           = 28
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           = 0
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           = 1
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           = 26 -
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           *
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           = -2
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           = 25
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           = 24
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = (Y + [Y/4] + M +
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           ) mod 7
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 6 (M = 6)
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 0 (M = 5)
          </td>
          <td>
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           = 6 (M = 3)
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           E =
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           −
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           **
          </td>
          <td>
           E = -8 April = 23 March
          </td>
          <td>
           E = 25 April
          </td>
          <td>
           E = 18 April
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="4">
           * Subtract 1 if
           <i>
            b
           </i>
           = 0 or 1. ** Add 31 if
           <i>
            c
           </i>
           -
           <i>
            d
           </i>
           &lt; 1.
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_algorithms">
        Other algorithms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Computus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other algorithms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Faster and more compact algorithms for Gregorian Easter Sunday exist.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otheralgs_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-otheralgs-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Software">
        Software
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Computus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Software">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">
         Perl
        </a>
        – Rich Bowen's
        <code>
         Date::Easter
        </code>
        module available from
        <a href="/wiki/CPAN" title="CPAN">
         CPAN
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
         <a href="#cite_note-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">
         Excel
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
         <a href="#cite_note-58">
          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>
        – Let cell
        <b>
         A1
        </b>
        contain a year ≥ 1900; format calculating cell as a date.
        <ul>
         <li>
          <code>
           =DOLLAR(("4/"&amp;
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           )/7+MOD(19*MOD(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           ,19)-7,30)*14%,)*7-6
          </code>
          for year 1900 – 2203 when the Excel date system is 190
          <b>
           0
          </b>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <code>
           =ROUND
           <b>
            (
           </b>
           DATE(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           ,4,1-DAY(0))/7+MOD(19*MOD(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           ,19)-7,30)*0.14,0
           <b>
            )
           </b>
           *7-6+DAY(0)
          </code>
          similar to above but independent of system local settings and date system.
         </li>
         <li>
          <code>
           =FLOOR((4&amp;-
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           )-DAY(5)+97%*MOD(18.998*MOD(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           +8/9,19)+INT(68%*INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           %)-INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           %/4)-5/9),30),7)+DAY(1)
          </code>
          provides the Gregorian Easter Sunday from 1900/1904 to 9999 in the Excel date systems 1900 and 1904.
         </li>
         <li>
          <code>
           =FLOOR(DATE(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           ,4,97%*MOD(18.998*MOD(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           +8/9,19)+INT(68%*INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           %)-INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           %/4)-5/9),30)-DAY(4)),7)+DAY(1)
          </code>
          similar to above, independent from the country specific order in the term
          <b>
           (4&amp;-A1)
          </b>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <code>
           =FLOOR
           <b>
            (
           </b>
           DATE(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           ,3,27-DAY(0))+0.97*MOD(18.998*MOD(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           +8/9,19)+INT(0.68*INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           /100)-INT(
           <b>
            A1
           </b>
           /400)-5/9),30),7
           <b>
            )
           </b>
           +DAY(1)
          </code>
          slightly different version of the one above, probably easier to comprehend.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Python – adapted from
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otheralgs_56-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-otheralgs-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
         <pre>
<span class="k">def</span> <span class="nf">IanTaylorEasterJscr</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">year</span><span class="p">):</span>
 <span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">19</span>
 <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span> <span class="mi">2</span>
 <span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">//</span> <span class="mi">25</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
 <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span> <span class="mi">2</span>
 <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">((</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="mi">19</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">((</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="mi">8</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">//</span> <span class="mi">25</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">15</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">30</span>
 <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">+=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">29578</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span> <span class="mi">10</span>
 <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">-=</span> <span class="p">((</span><span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">7</span>
 <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span> <span class="mi">5</span>
 <span class="n">day</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="mi">31</span>
 <span class="n">month</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">3</span>
 <span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">year</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">month</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">day</span>
</pre>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/BASIC" title="BASIC">
         BASIC
        </a>
        – This is a version with the algorithm from Gauss, Zeller, Lichtenberg et al.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
         <a href="#cite_note-59">
          [59]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <br/>
        This code is only valid for years in the Gregorian calendar. For the Julian calendar set K = 0, S = 0, R = 0.
        <div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
         <pre>
<span class="k">Function</span> <span class="nf">Easter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="c">' X = year to compute</span>
 <span class="k">Dim</span> <span class="n">K</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">M</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">S</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">A</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">D</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">R</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">OG</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">SZ</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">OE</span>

 <span class="n">K</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">X</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">100</span> <span class="c">' Secular number</span>
 <span class="n">M</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">15</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">K</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">4</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">8</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">K</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">13</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">25</span> <span class="c">' Secular Moon shift</span>
 <span class="n">S</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">2</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">K</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">4</span> <span class="c">' Secular Sun shift</span>
 <span class="n">A</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">X</span> <span class="ow">Mod</span> <span class="mi">19</span> <span class="c">' Moon parameter</span>
 <span class="n">D</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">19</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">A</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">M</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="ow">Mod</span> <span class="mi">30</span> <span class="c">' Seed for 1st full Moon in spring</span>
 <span class="n">R</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">D</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">A</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">11</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">29</span> <span class="c">' Calendarian correction quantity (Lichtenberg's improvement of the original: R = D \ 29 + (D \ 28 - D \ 29) * (A \ 11))</span>
 <span class="n">OG</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">21</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">D</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">R</span> <span class="c">' Easter limit</span>
 <span class="n">SZ</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">X</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">X</span> <span class="o">\</span> <span class="mi">4</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">S</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="ow">Mod</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="c">' 1st Sunday in March</span>
 <span class="n">OE</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">OG</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">SZ</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="ow">Mod</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="c">' Distance Easter Sunday from Easter limit in days</span>

 

<span class="k">End</span> <span class="k">Function</span>
</pre>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">
         Java
        </a>
        – Anonymous (also called Meeus/Jones/Butcher) Gregorian algorithm.
        <br/>
        This code is only valid for years in the Gregorian calendar.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
       <pre>
<span class="kd">public</span> <span class="kd">static</span> <span class="n">Date</span> <span class="nf">getEasterDate</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">year</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">{</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">19</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">f</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">8</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">25</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">g</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">f</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">3</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="mi">19</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">g</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">15</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">30</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">k</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">l</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="mi">32</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">k</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">11</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">22</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">l</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">451</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">l</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">31</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="kt">int</span> <span class="n">p</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">(</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">l</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span> <span class="o">*</span> <span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="o">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">31</span><span class="o">;</span>
	<span class="n">Calendar</span> <span class="n">calendar</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">GregorianCalendar</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="na">getInstance</span><span class="o">();</span>
	<span class="n">calendar</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="na">clear</span><span class="o">();</span>
	<span class="n">calendar</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="na">set</span><span class="o">(</span><span class="n">year</span><span class="o">,</span> <span class="n">n</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="o">,</span> <span class="n">p</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="o">);</span>
	<span class="k">return</span> <span class="n">calendar</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="na">getTime</span><span class="o">();</span>
<span class="o">}</span>
</pre>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MS-SQL" title="MS-SQL">
         MS-SQL
        </a>
        based on the Meeus/Jones/Butcher algorithm above.
        <div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
         <pre>
<span class="k">DROP</span> <span class="n">FUNCTION</span> <span class="p">[</span><span class="n">dbo</span><span class="p">].[</span><span class="n">fn_getEasterDate</span><span class="p">]</span>
<span class="n">GO</span>

<span class="k">CREATE</span> <span class="n">FUNCTION</span> <span class="p">[</span><span class="n">dbo</span><span class="p">].[</span><span class="n">fn_getEasterDate</span><span class="p">]</span> <span class="p">(</span>
	<span class="o">@</span><span class="n">xYear</span> <span class="kt">int</span>
<span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">RETURNS</span> <span class="kt">date</span>
<span class="k">AS</span>
<span class="n">BEGIN</span>
	<span class="cm">/*Calculate date of easter based on Year passed*/</span>
	<span class="cm">/*Based on Anonymous Gregorian Algorithm, also known as the Meeus/Jones/Butcher algorithm*/</span>
	<span class="k">Declare</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">dGregorianEaster</span> <span class="kt">date</span>
	<span class="k">Declare</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">d</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">e</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">f</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">g</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">i</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">k</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">L</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">m</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">month</span> <span class="kt">int</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">day</span> <span class="kt">int</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">xYear</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">19</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">xyear</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">xYear</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">100</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">f</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">((</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">8</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">25</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">g</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">((</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">f</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">/</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">19</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">b</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">d</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">g</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">15</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">30</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">k</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">c</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">L</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">e</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">i</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">k</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">7</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">((</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">a</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">11</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">22</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">L</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">451</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">month</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">floor</span><span class="p">((</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">L</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">31</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">day</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">h</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">L</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="o">*@</span><span class="n">m</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">31</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span>
	<span class="kt">set</span> <span class="o">@</span><span class="n">dGregorianEaster</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nf">cast</span><span class="p">(</span> <span class="nf">cast</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">xYear</span> <span class="k">as</span> <span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">))</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="s1">'-'</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="k">right</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'0'</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nf">cast</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">month</span> <span class="k">as</span> <span class="kt">varchar</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)),</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">+</span> <span class="s1">'-'</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="k">right</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'0'</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nf">cast</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">day</span> <span class="k">as</span> <span class="kt">varchar</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)),</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="k">as</span> <span class="kt">date</span><span class="p">)</span>
	<span class="k">RETURN</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">@</span><span class="n">dGregorianEaster</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">END</span>
<span class="n">GO</span>
<span class="k">select</span> <span class="n">dbo</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nf">fn_getEasterDate</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1961</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="k">select</span> <span class="n">dbo</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nf">fn_getEasterDate</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2014</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/PL/SQL" title="PL/SQL">
         PL/SQL
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
       <pre>
<span class="k">CREATE</span> <span class="k">OR</span> <span class="k">REPLACE</span> <span class="k">FUNCTION</span> <span class="n">easter_sunday</span><span class="p">(</span> <span class="n">_year</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="p">)</span> <span class="k">RETURNS</span> <span class="nb">DATE</span>
 <span class="k">LANGUAGE</span> <span class="n">PLPGSQL</span> <span class="k">IMMUTABLE</span> <span class="k">STRICT</span> <span class="n">LEAKPROOF</span> 
 <span class="k">SECURITY</span> <span class="k">INVOKER</span>
 <span class="n">COST</span> <span class="mi">50</span>
<span class="k">AS</span> <span class="err">$</span><span class="k">function</span><span class="err">$</span>
 <span class="cm">/*</span>
<span class="cm"> * Title: The date of Easter</span>
<span class="cm"> * Authors: Downing, A. M. W.</span>
<span class="cm"> * Journal: The Observatory, Vol. 39, p. 215-219 (1916)</span>
<span class="cm"> * Bibliographic Code: 1916Obs....39..215D</span>
<span class="cm"> * http://articles.adsabs.harvard.edu//full/1916Obs....39..215D/0000215.000.html</span>
<span class="cm"> * refers to Nature, 1876 April 20, vol. 13, p. 487 for the algorithm.</span>
<span class="cm"> * NB. Neither this author nor the anonymous 1876 contributor have provided a proof</span>
<span class="cm"> * of this algorithm's correctness, but testing has revealed no problems.</span>
<span class="cm"> */</span>
 <span class="k">DECLARE</span>
 <span class="n">AA</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">_year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">19</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- A=YEAR%19</span>
 <span class="n">BB</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">_year</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- B=YEAR/100</span>
 <span class="n">CC</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">_year</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- C=YEAR%100</span>
 <span class="n">DD</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">BB</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- D=B/4</span>
 <span class="n">EE</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">BB</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- E=B%4</span>
 <span class="n">FF</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">BB</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">8</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">25</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- F=(B+8)/25</span>
 <span class="n">GG</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">BB</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">FF</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- G=(B-F+1)/3</span>
 <span class="n">HH</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">19</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">AA</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">BB</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">DD</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">GG</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">15</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">30</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- H=(19*A+B-D-G+15)%30</span>
 <span class="n">II</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">CC</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- I=C/4</span>
 <span class="n">KK</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="n">CC</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- K=C%4</span>
 <span class="n">LL</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">EE</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">II</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">HH</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="n">KK</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- L=(32+2*E+2*I-H-K)%7</span>
 <span class="n">MM</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">AA</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">11</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">HH</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">22</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">LL</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">451</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- M=(A+11*H+22*L)/451</span>
 <span class="n">NN</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">HH</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">LL</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">MM</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">/</span> <span class="mi">31</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- N=(H+L-7*M+114)/31</span>
 <span class="n">OO</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span> <span class="k">DEFAULT</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">HH</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="n">LL</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="mi">7</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">MM</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">114</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">%</span> <span class="mi">31</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- O=(H+L-7*M+114)%31</span>
 <span class="n">EM</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- Easter month [3, 4]</span>
 <span class="n">ED</span> <span class="nb">INTEGER</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- Easter date (within the month)</span>
 <span class="k">BEGIN</span>
 <span class="n">EM</span> <span class="p">:</span><span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">NN</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- Easter Month [3=March, 4=April]</span>
 <span class="n">ED</span> <span class="p">:</span><span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">OO</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="c1">-- Easter Date [date in Easter Month]</span>
 <span class="k">RETURN</span> <span class="n">make_date</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="n">_year</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">EM</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">ED</span><span class="p">);</span>
 <span class="k">END</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="err">$</span><span class="k">function</span><span class="err">$</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="k">SELECT</span> <span class="n">easter_sunday</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1954</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="c1">-- should return 1954-04-18</span>
<span class="k">SELECT</span> <span class="n">easter_sunday</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2016</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="c1">-- should return 2016-03-27</span>
</pre>
      </div>

        <li id="cite_note-9">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-9">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The lunar cycle of Anatolius, according to the tables in
          <i>
           De ratione paschali
          </i>
          , included only two bissextile (leap) years every 19 years, so could not be used by anyone using the Julian calendar, which had four or five leap years per lunar cycle. See C.H. Turner, "
          <a class="external text" href="http://ehr.oxfordjournals.org/cgi/content/citation/X/XL/699" rel="nofollow">
           The Paschal Canon of Anatolius of Laodicea
          </a>
          ",
          <i>
           The English Historical Review
          </i>
          <b>
           10
          </b>
          (1895) 699–710, or Daniel McCarthy, "
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.springerlink.com/content/l8672t43w8647546/" rel="nofollow">
           The Lunar and Paschal Tables of
           <i>
            De ratione paschali
           </i>
           Attributed to Anatolius of Laodicea
          </a>
          ",
          <i>
           Archive for History of Exact Sciences
          </i>
          <b>
           49
          </b>
          (1995–96) 285–320.
         </span>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Search.cpan.org&amp;rft.atitle=Date%3A%3AEaster&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fsearch.cpan.org%2F~rbow%2FDate-Easter-1.14%2Flib%2FDate%2FEaster.pm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComputus">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-58">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-58">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.contextures.com/exceleastercalculation.html" rel="nofollow">
           Contextures – Excel Easter Date Calculations.
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-59">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

            ^
           </a>

         <span class="reference-text">

           <a class="external text" href="http://www.ptb.de/cms/en/fachabteilungen/abt4/fb-44/ag-441/realisation-of-legal-time-in-germany/the-date-of-easter.html" rel="nofollow">
            "The date of Easter"
           </a>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Physikalisch-Technische_Bundesanstalt" title="Physikalisch-Technische Bundesanstalt">
            Physikalisch-Technische Bundesanstalt

            . Retrieved

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+date+of+Easter&amp;rft.pub=Physikalisch-Technische+Bundesanstalt+%28PTB%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ptb.de%2Fcms%2Fen%2Ffachabteilungen%2Fabt4%2Ffb-44%2Fag-441%2Frealisation-of-legal-time-in-germany%2Fthe-date-of-easter.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AComputus">
           <span style="display:none;">
